Local News

Japanese Sailors

Robbing Inspectors

Japanese Goods Seized at Huatong Wharf

Taken Away by Japanese Soldiers Midway

It Is Agreed to Use Armed Escorts in the Future

Since the Anti-Japanese Association sent personnel to inspect Japanese goods at various wharf, smuggling of Japanese goods has often been seized. The night before last (i.e. the 12th), the inspectors again seized a large batch of Japanese cloth and cotton yarn at the Huatong Wharf in Pudong, which was shipped from Niuzhuang. The inspectors detained all the goods, but the Japanese ordered Japanese soldiers to seize them by force and rob four inspectors, who were beaten and humiliated by the Japanese along the way. This matter has now been protested by our side. The detailed information of this matter is truthfully reported as follows:

First Smuggling Seizure On the 4th of this month, Japanese merchants such as Jiangshang Ito in Shanghai each had a large batch of Oriental cloth and cotton yarn, a total of 360 pieces, and entrusted the Japanese transportation company International Association to declare them to Niuzhuang. Because no Japanese ships were sailing on this route, they were transferred to Taikoo Company's Daming Wheel. However, when Daming returned the goods due to too many cargoes, it was changed to De'an Wheel for transportation. During the transfer to the ship, the Anti-Japanese Association learned about it and urgently sent an inspection team to the port to inspect it. The batch of 360 pieces of cloth and yarn, worth more than 70,000 taels of silver, were detained and taken to Lujiazui. When the Japanese merchants learned about it, they wanted to recover it. At that time, the Japanese goods had already been put into the warehouse. The Japanese consulate raised this matter with our side, but it has not been resolved yet. The second batch of Japanese goods continued to be loaded and was seized again.

Second Seizure of Japanese Goods On the 12th, the Oriental Cotton Yarn Association in Shanghai had 171 pieces of cloth and yarn, worth 33,185 taels of silver, which were also destined for Yingkou. It was also entrusted to the International Transportation Association to declare them. They were loaded onto Taikoo Company's Lin'an Wheel to Niuzhuang. This batch of goods was loaded onto a barge by a small steamer to Huatong Wharf in Pudong at 7:00 PM on the 12th. It did not start until about 9:00 PM to load into the Lin'an ship. After two hours, more than 90 pieces had been loaded, and about 80 pieces were still being loaded. When the inspection team of the Anti-Japanese Association arrived at the port by small steamer, after discovering these Japanese goods, they ordered the coolies to stop loading. At the same time, they ordered the receiver on the Lin'an ship to unload the more than 90 pieces that had already entered the cabin and put them back on the original barge. Then the inspectors detained all the goods and used this wheel to tow them to Lujiazui to report to the association for verification.

Japanese Merchants Send Soldiers to Seize Goods This time the Japanese merchants transferred these goods. Dongmian transferred Konemoto Seitaro and International sent Hayashida to the dock to supervise the loading of the goods. When the inspectors detained the goods, both Japanese were not present. It was not until after 10:00 that the goods had been taken away by the inspection team when the Japanese Hayashida arrived and saw this situation. He immediately rushed to the Japanese Marine Corps in Yuanhai and requested to send troops to protect them. The Japanese naval commander informed the Ataka warship stationed in the Huangpu River and sent 25 fully armed Japanese marines, accompanied by Hayashida, to Pudong. They immediately took the Zuifeng Maru small wheel and chased after them. The inspection team's small wheel was slow because it was dragging a heavy cargo barge, so it had just arrived at Lujiazui and was about to enter the port when the Japanese soldiers arrived, seized the original goods and barge, and towed them away by the Zuifeng Maru small wheel.

Japanese Soldiers Rob and Plunder Inspectors When the Japanese soldiers chased to the inspection team's small steamer, they jumped into the boat with weapons. On the one hand, they seized the cargo barge, and on the other hand, they used guns to beat the inspectors on the boat. Most of our inspectors were unarmed, how could they resist the fully armed Japanese soldiers? Moreover, the Japanese soldiers were determined to seek a reward and beat anyone they saw. The inspectors rushed ashore to take temporary shelter. Song Zhiwen, Gao Shanlin, Wang Ajin, Wang Meifa, and others were caught by the Japanese soldiers, dragged onto the Japanese's Zuifeng Maru small wheel, and kidnapped away. After boarding the wheel, the Japanese soldiers beat the four people with their gun butts, first押 them to the Ataka warship, and then the Japanese soldiers transferred them to the Japanese Consulate by warship small wheel.

Negotiations by the Public Security Bureau After this incident occurred, the Anti-Japanese Association has reported to the Municipal Government. Yesterday noon, the Shanghai Public Security Bureau has sent personnel to the Japanese Consulate to negotiate the release of the inspectors Song Gao Wang Wang, who were kidnapped and押 by the Japanese soldiers. It is heard that the inspectors have been領 back yesterday noon and will file another negotiation.

Japanese Merchants Meet to Discuss Loading Goods Yesterday, the Japanese merchants in Shanghai went to the Japanese Consulate to hold a meeting to discuss the transportation methods of Japanese goods in the future. As a result of the discussion, the Japanese believed that it was most appropriate to use force to deal with the Anti-Japanese Association's inspection of goods. The Japanese merchants cited the success of the Japanese soldiers recovering 20麻袋s in Suzhou River and the success of recovering more than 170 pieces of cloth and yarn this time. In the future, the loading and transportation of Japanese goods will be protected by armed navy. If there is any inspection and detention of goods, the Japanese soldiers will be allowed to act freely. It is heard that the Japanese Consul and the Naval Authorities have all tacitly agreed, so yesterday, all the Japanese merchants were full of ambition and expressed that they were not afraid of anti-Japanese sentiment and that the transportation of goods would become an open loading. This move is closely related to the future of our anti-Japanese sentiment.

Declaration of the Committee To the compatriots across the country, unfortunately, our country has been repeatedly invaded by foreign enemies. The Japanese imperialists have not only seized our fields and occupied our land in Wanbaoshan, killed our farmers, and insulted our officials, but also instigated rioters in Korea to massacre our overseas Chinese. In just ten days, more than 1,000 people have died, thousands have been injured, and property worth tens of millions of yuan has been lost. However, the Japanese imperialists have no remorse. The Japanese warships stationed in Shanghai have repeatedly sent armed navy to invade the Chinese boundary, rob goods, and arrest compatriots, and beat and injure the staff of this association. Their treacherous intentions, tyrannical behavior, and despicable tactics are truly unbearable for us. Now, the facts of the incident are reported to the people of the country for your consideration. At 5:00 AM on the 11th of this month, the Zhabei Inspection Office of this association received a report that a奸商 had purchased 7,500 Japanese麻袋s and was trying to smuggle them out of the country on Suzhou Road. The Inspection Office immediately sent personnel to intercept them. At 8:00 AM, a person claiming to be Japanese came forward to interfere and requested their return. The Inspection Office had no right to return them and immediately accompanied the Japanese to this association to request that the association return the goods if they were purchased by the Japanese after verification. Personnel were immediately sent to the dock to verify them as soon as possible. Unexpectedly, the staff of this association had just arrived at the dock when the detained麻袋s were forcibly robbed by armed soldiers. According to eyewitnesses at the time, at 12:00 noon that morning, more than 30 Japanese soldiers suddenly came, fully armed, as if facing a major enemy. The muzzles of their guns were aimed at the inspection boat, forbidding the guards from speaking. At the same time, more than 10 Japanese soldiers carried the麻袋s into a small steamer and roared away. The day after this incident occurred, the Pudong Inspection Office of this association discovered that a奸商 had purchased Japanese yarn and was transporting it to other ports, so it immediately sent personnel to detain it in the Huangpu River and hired another small wheel to tow it back to Pudong. When it reached the Jiang'an shore, there was a Japanese ship full of Japanese soldiers lying in ambush, who completely robbed the yarn and abducted our inspectors Song Zhiwen, Gao Shanlin, Wang Meifa, Wang Ajin, and four others. One person's whereabouts are unknown, and his life or death is uncertain. At about 2:00 AM that night, this association received a report and immediately sent cadres to the Public Security Bureau to negotiate. After several twists and turns, the Japanese Consulate sent the four abducted persons back to this association at 12:00 noon. As for the missing person, there is still no news of him, and his life or death is uncertain. The four released persons were either kicked by leather shoes or beaten by gun butts, so that their arms, legs, waists, and backs were all covered in blood stains and scars. Looking at them, we could not help but sob. The colleagues of this association, in the face of national crisis, are entrusted with heavy responsibilities by all sectors of society. They are willing to go through fire and water, and they will have no regrets even if they die. They only think that China is the China of 400 million people, and saving the country is a public matter of 400 million people. Everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the world. The colleagues of this association should go forward bravely and take the lead. All sectors of the country should also rise up and stand up, and our high-ranking party and government organs, who usually lead the people and devote themselves to the revolution of the Three Principles of the People, should also share the same hatred and be pioneers for the people. Today, the Japanese imperialists have seized our national land, killed our overseas Chinese, and the Japanese warships stationed in Shanghai have sent large teams of Japanese soldiers to invade the Chinese boundary, kidnap people, and rob goods. If this is not done, what is not done? If this can be tolerated, what cannot be tolerated? The five-minute enthusiasm is very shameful, but if even this five-minute enthusiasm does not exist, will it not be even more shameful? Alas, it is better to die without freedom. Now, fight for freedom or die. Do not fight or die. Is there still a place for our Chinese people who are willing to give up on themselves in the beautiful rivers and mountains of 40,000 square miles? Why do the people of the country still cling to this dream of being a slave of all nations and not be the vanguard of the times? Soong Ching Ling Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Going Directly to the Soong Residence on Seymour Road to Mourn

Deciding on Future Actions After the Funeral

Madame Soong Ching Ling, accompanied by her secretary Ms. Hu Lanqi, returned to China from Berlin to mourn her mother. She arrived at the port on the Dalian Maru at 6:20 PM yesterday. She landed at the Huangpu Wharf and took a car directly to the Soong residence on Seymour Road to rest. Those who came to Shanghai on the same wheel as Madame Sun included Zhou Xiangxian, the secretary of the General Headquarters sent by Chairman Chiang to Liaoning to welcome her, and Shi Xiaofeng of the Lizi Society, a total of four people.

Welcome at the Wharf Those who went to the Huangpu Wharf to welcome her yesterday included the newly appointed Ambassador to Japan Chiang Tso-pin, Mayor Zhang Qun, Vice Minister of Industry Zheng Hongnian, President of Jiaotong University Li Zhaohuan, Superintendent of Jianghai Customs Tang Hai'an, Madame Lian Shenghai, wife of the Vice Minister of Railways, Soong Tzu-liang, and the two daughters of Kung Hsiang-hsi, and dozens of others. Jiang Yi, the deputy officer of the Garrison Headquarters, led members of the investigation team and personally took care of everything at the wharf. The Municipal Public Security Bureau sent about 20 officers of the water police and plainclothes police, and the police also sent many Chinese and Western detectives to guard everything. She shook hands with Chiang Tso-pin and Madame Lian Shenghai and hurried off the wheel. She walked extremely fast and did not say a word to the reporters. After leaving the wharf fence, she took the car prepared by the Kung residence and went directly to the Soong residence on Seymour Road to mourn. Kung Hsiang-hsi's two daughters and Soong Tzu-liang and others were in the same car as Madame Sun.

Madame's Appearance Madame Sun wore a snuff-colored Western-style coat, a Western-style hat, deeply pressed against her eyebrows. Her leather shoes and silk stockings were the same color as her coat. She was in good spirits and her appearance was slightly more plump than when she last came to Shanghai. After Madame Sun arrived at the Soong residence, she performed a silent prayer in front of the coffin of Mother Soong in the hall. Soong Ai-ling, Soong Mei-ling, Soong Tzu-wen, Tzu-liang, Tzu-an, and others were all present to perform the ceremony.

Staying in Shanghai Briefly According to sources around her, Madame Sun came here specifically to mourn her mother. After Mother Soong's funeral is over, she plans to stay in Shanghai for a while before deciding on her next course of action. She is currently staying temporarily on Seymour Road and will not move to her residence on Molier Road. It is also rumored that Mr. Zhang Minyi came with Madame Sun, which is not true. Zhang is an engineer and has already landed in Qingdao.

Interview with the Secretary A reporter from the New Voice Society interviewed Ms. Hu Lanqi, the former member of the Jiangxi Provincial Government who came with Madame Sun as her secretary. She said that Madame Sun and others left Berlin on the 31st of last month and came here specifically to mourn her mother. I don't know whether she will return to Germany in the future. In Germany, she often studies in the library and studies the last words of the Premier. Roughly speaking, Madame Sun will publish the collected and supplemented遺著 of the Premier.

Mother Soong's Funeral Scheduled

Zhang Qun Publicly Elected as Director of Funeral Affairs

Ordinary Instruments of Ceremony Are Dismissed

According to the news from the funeral office of Mother Soong Ni, it has been decided to issue the invitation on August 17th and hold the funeral on the 18th. Chairman Chiang cannot come to Shanghai at that time due to the emergency of suppressing the Communist army. From 8:00 AM to 6:00 PM on the 17th, individuals can pay their respects at any time. The funeral office has publicly elected Mayor Zhang as the director of funeral affairs, Director of Public Security Chen Xizeng as the commander-in-chief, and Vice Minister of Finance Li Diaosheng as the director of reception. The funeral route is planned from Seymour Road, through Nanyang Road, to Xiaosha Ferry Road, to Jing'an Temple Road, through Da Xi Road, and Zhongshan Avenue, to Hongqiao Road, and to the International Cemetery. From 5:30 AM to 8:00 PM on that day, strict security will be enforced, and vehicles will be temporarily stopped when the hearse passes by, and idlers will be prohibited. Ordinary instruments of ceremony will not be used, and the army band will lead the hearse. All those who hold the紼 to see off the funeral must wear black纱 around their arms and commemorative badges on their lapels. The funeral office will designate a meeting place. Assemble at 8:00 AM and follow the hearse when it passes by, or follow by car, or go directly to the location. They will perform the ceremony at that time and then disperse. In addition to the badges prepared separately for internal staff, those who intend to hold the紼 to see off the funeral, in addition to relatives and friends who receive them from the mourning host, must have the leaders of various groups and organizations send a list to the funeral office before August 16th to receive them in advance.

Inspection Team Arrives in Shanghai

A Total of Twenty-One People

The Los Angeles Chamber of Commerce in the United States has specially organized a Far East Commercial Inspection Team to inspect business conditions in Japan and China. The members of the team are all important business figures in the city. The leader of the team is Mr. Clarence Matson, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce. Matson leads 20 team members, all of whom are bankers, transporters, engineers, navigators, and stock traders, such as Boyli, James, Via Sai, and Dewey, etc. They arrived in Japan from San Francisco and, after completing their inspection in the East, took the Nagasaki Maru Wheel of the Japan Mail Company from Kobe to Shanghai yesterday. They arrived in Shen at about 3:00 PM and landed at the Huishan Wharf. After all the team members arrived in Shanghai, all reception and guidance matters were handled by the Transportation Bank. They are now staying in hotels and will stay in Shanghai for a few days before going to the capital for sightseeing.

French Merchant Tram and Bus

Yesterday All Stopped

Eight People Injured Due to Worker Conflict

Machine Department Resumes Work, Transportation Department Halts Again

Formal Traffic Resumes That Evening, Full Resumption Today

Yesterday, a conflict occurred between the machine department and transportation department workers of the French Water and Electricity Company. The machine department workers immediately went on strike, and all trams and buses in the French Concession were stopped. By noon, the machine department issue was resolved, and work resumed uniformly in the afternoon. However, the transportation department workers were unwilling to work and went on strike together. The transportation department issue was also resolved by 6 p.m. At 6:30 p.m., the tram and bus workers on all routes formally resumed work, making a single round trip before returning to the depot. Formal work resumption begins today. The authorities have also sent personnel to thoroughly investigate. The various circumstances of yesterday are recorded separately below.

Truth of the Conflict: Qian Ashun, a worker in the lathe shop of the machine department, was walking along the Bund on Avenue Edward VII at 7:20 a.m. yesterday, preparing to take a tram to the factory for work. He bent down to pick up a copper coin that had fallen to the ground. At that moment, Route 2 tram heading to Xujiahui was coming from the 16th Pier. Seeing the worker in front, it immediately braked. The driver used discourteous language, leading to a conflict. Driver Sun Yinglong of tram No. 221, ticket seller Zhang Guisheng of first-class tram No. 35, ticket seller Shi Shiyong of third-class tram No. 361, and ticket seller Gu Yuewen of trailer No. 381 got out of the trams one after another and started beating the worker. As a result, the worker sustained minor internal injuries and immediately went to the factory to report to his fellow workers in the department.

Machine Workers' Strike: More than 1,200 staff and workers in over twenty departments of the machine department, including the lathe shop, waterworks, engineering department, painters, fire department, wiring department, large warehouse, carpenters, motor department, Dongjiadu waterworks, and railway engine department, were extremely angered. They immediately went on strike automatically at 8 a.m. In addition to holding a meeting to discuss countermeasures through the union, they also dispatched inspectors to drive the company's own prepared trams to various locations to dissuade all trams from running, forcing them into the Lujiiawan depot and detaining the offending driver No. 221 and ticket seller No. 35 in the machine department for temporary custody.

Emergency Meeting: The First District Water and Electricity Industry Union immediately held an emergency meeting and resolved on the spot to propose: (1) The transportation department shall set off firecrackers to the machine department to express apology; (2) The offending driver and ticket seller shall be dismissed from their positions, and Inspector Li Linshu of Route 2 shall be dismissed from office; (3) The company shall issue a notice to ensure that similar incidents do not occur again in the future; (4) The company shall issue a notice to prohibit drivers and ticket sellers of all trams from beating people, and nominate representatives such as Zhang Renjun, Lu Guanhong, and Xu A’mei to negotiate seriously with the company.

All Trams Stopped: Yesterday at about 9 a.m., more than 80 trams on Routes 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 10 and trolleybuses on Routes 18 and 17 and buses on Routes 21 and 22 in the French Concession were stopped by the machine department workers. They gathered in places such as Lujiiawan and the 16th Pier. Over 80 trams were parked from Xiejiao to Lujiiawan, and from Route Lafayette to the Lujiiawan area. There were also over 10 trams at the 16th Pier. All buses were stopped near Lujiiawan, disrupting traffic.

Machine Department Resumes Work: At around 10 a.m., the machine department sent representatives Xu A’mei, Lu Guanhong, and Zhang Renjun, etc., based on the workers'

Page 14

demands, to negotiate with Manager Monsalant (transliteration) and Chinese Director Du Yuesheng at the company in Lujiiawan. As a result: (1) They purchased 100 yuan worth of firecrackers to express apology; (2) If Inspector Li Linshu of Route 2 is indeed the leader, he will be dismissed from office; (3) The company will issue a notice prohibiting future incidents; (4) The company will post notices in each tram prohibiting ticket sellers and drivers from beating people. The representatives immediately went to the factory to report the negotiation progress. All the workers considered it satisfactory. Dong Guixiang then took a car to Baxianqiao to buy firecrackers. From 12:10 to 12:20 p.m., the sound of firecrackers was incessant from Baxianqiao to Routes Avenue Joffre and Route Pichon. All the machine department workers immediately went home for lunch, and uniformly returned to the factory in the afternoon to resume work.

Setting Off Firecrackers: The 100 yuan worth of firecrackers totaled 500 large cannons (firecrackers of considerable size), and over 100,000 small firecrackers. When they were set off together, the general residents of the French Concession were extremely frightened by the sound, mistaking it for gunfire. The Nanhua sub-bureau authorities in Lujiiawan also sent police to guard the factory. A small shed in the factory caught fire while the firecrackers were being set off. Carried by the wind, it suddenly burned down at 2 p.m., and was completely destroyed in less than five minutes.

Company Prohibition: The management office of the French Water and Electricity Company issued a notice yesterday stating: "Recently, verbal disputes and physical altercations have frequently occurred between the personnel of the machine department and transportation department. This kind of behavior is extremely detrimental to the company's business operations. The manager hereby sincerely advises all company personnel to refrain from such behavior in the future. Anyone who causes further incidents will be severely punished. This is hereby announced."

Authorities' Investigation: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau heard yesterday that all the tram and bus routes of the French Water and Electricity Company had been shut down, disrupting traffic. It immediately sent Zhu Guilin to investigate the truth. Upon learning that it was caused by a conflict between the transportation department and machine department workers and not a labor-capital dispute, he immediately reported the circumstances.

Mutual Assault and Injuries: When the trams and buses of the transportation department returned to the depot, a major conflict occurred between all the drivers, ticket sellers, inspectors, and staff of the transportation department and the workers of the machine department at the gate of the Lujiiawan depot, followed by physical violence. It was reported that Inspector Wu Qishu of Route 2, driver Sun Yinglong of Route 23, ticket seller Zhu Wanjin of Route 7, ticket seller Liu Fusheng of Route 13, ticket seller Sun Hengzhi of Route 170, ticket seller Shi Yingfu of Route 196, and a new ticket seller of Route 203 all sustained minor injuries and were sent to the Guangci Hospital on Rue du Père Robert by the transportation department.

Unwilling to Drive: All 800 staff and workers of the transportation department felt defeated. Afterward, they were all unwilling to work. At 1 p.m., they held an emergency meeting at the Transportation Department Club on Route Massenet and resolved: (1) The coppersmith is to publish an apology in the newspaper and set off firecrackers; (2) The company will punish the offenders responsible; (3) The machine department is to bear the responsibility for medical expenses and the future risks of those who were beaten; (4) Guarantee that such unfortunate incidents will not occur again in the future. Five representatives were nominated: ticket seller Cai Hongjun of Route 38, ticket seller Yan Youqing of Route 254, ticket seller Zhong Runsheng of Route 69, ticket seller Li Xinzhai of Route 178, and driver Zhang Wenming of Route 49 to negotiate with the company.

Meeting with Du Yuesheng: The machine department workers, i.e., the First District Water and Electricity Industry Union, heard that the transportation department workers were going to cause trouble. At 3 p.m., they sent Xu A’mei, Zhang Renjun, Lu Guanhong, Ding Yougen and four others to Du Yuesheng's private residence to request protection. Du Yuesheng replied to the machine workers that they could continue to work as usual and that the strike of the transportation department workers had nothing to do with the machine department and he would be responsible for their protection.

Negotiation Results: Yesterday at 6 p.m., Transportation Department representatives Cai Hongjun, Yan Youqing, Zhang Wenhong, Zhong Runsheng, Li Xinzhai and other five representatives negotiated with Manager Monsalant and Comprador Shen in the company based on the conditions proposed by the workers. As a result: (1) The company will purchase 100 yuan worth of firecrackers to set off as an apology; (2) Work will resume immediately; (3) The company will provide a concrete answer to all conditions before the 18th.

Formal Work Resumption: At 6:30 p.m., the sound of firecrackers rang out loudly in front of the Lujiiawan depot. By 6:45 p.m., all the trams and buses started up and made a round trip as a formal work resumption. By 7 p.m., they all returned to the depot. Full work resumption will commence tomorrow. Nearby residents were full of doubts and worries again.

County Government Recruiting Midwifery Students

The Shanghai County Government has received an order from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, instructing the county to recruit two female students for the Midwifery School attached to the Jiangsu Provincial Hospital for study at the school. It also approved the Jiangsu Provincial Hospital's notification that the Midwifery School would begin classes on September 1. The county may send two students without entrance examination, except for the Chinese language examination, in order to avoid future differences in level. It is requested that the resume and name list of each student be sent to the school by August 15 for registration, and tuition fees will be paid upon enrollment. Yesterday, the county government copied the regulations and posted them for recruitment. Those interested in studying should immediately prepare two 4-inch half-length photos, bring their previous academic certificates or transcripts to the county for registration, and wait for examination and recommendation.

Western Food Industry Workers

Struck Work the Day Before Yesterday Afternoon

Because the Capitalists Lack Sincerity in Accepting the Conditions

L'Aiglon, Hainssen, etc. Close Down in Succession

More than 300 workers in the Western food industry in this city automatically went on strike the day before yesterday afternoon because they saw that the capitalists were not sincere in accepting the conditions of treatment. L'Aiglon, Hainssen, and others had no choice but to temporarily close down. The Social Affairs Bureau persuaded the workers to resume work first. The various circumstances are recorded separately below.

Reasons for the Strike: The Western Food Industry Union, in a resolution passed by a members' meeting on May 6, proposed seven conditions of treatment. On July 27, it submitted them to the Western Food Industry Trade Association, setting a deadline for a concrete reply by 1 p.m. on July 30. When the deadline arrived without a reply, it nominated four representatives, Yao Shutang, Zhao Jinhua, Fu A’lian, and Wu Shenxiang, to negotiate with three representatives of the Trade Association, Wu Furen, Lin Zugen, and Lu Dechang. As a result, it was agreed that the Trade Association would reply by 11 p.m. on August 5 after a meeting and consultation. When the deadline arrived, the capitalists stated that they would reply in two weeks. The workers considered them to be insincere in accepting the conditions and resolved to hold a members' meeting on August 6, sending a letter to the Trade Association setting a deadline for a reply by August 8. When the deadline arrived, the capitalists ignored it. All the workers then implemented an automatic strike at 1 p.m. the day before yesterday (August 12).

A Few Close Down: Western Food companies such as Quan Jia Fu temporarily hired non-members of the Shanghai Western Food Industry Union to work in order to maintain business due to the workers' strike. However, Western food restaurants such as L'Aiglon and Hainssen were forced to temporarily close down due to the workers' strike. Regular patrons of Western food became alarmed.

Authorities' Investigation: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau received a petition from the union stating that the workers had automatically gone on strike and requesting mediation. It immediately sent Zhang Shuye to investigate the truth and persuaded the workers to resume work immediately and await mediation by the authorities in accordance with the law. The Western Food Industry Trade Association also sent all its directors and supervisors to persuade the workers to resume work uniformly today. However, because the workers felt that the capitalists' oppression was too severe, it is still difficult to determine whether work can be resumed today.

Disputed Conditions: The conditions of treatment proposed by the Western Food Industry Union are as follows: (1) The monthly small accounts of each Western food company must be calculated according to the total number of businesses each month, and the distribution must be made public. They must not be reported as more or less. Incidental expenses should also not be included in the account. Those who create various pretexts and workers who do not serve in the store shall not be eligible for this small account. The small accounts obtained by each store's assistant manager shall not exceed three shares; (2) Extra bonuses must not be enjoyed by capitalists, assistant managers, and accounting clerks; (3) One share of the monthly small accounts of each Western food company must be taken from the total amount to be used as a subsidy for the union; (4) The wages of each worker must be calculated as double wages in January, February, July, and August of the Gregorian calendar. Those who should take a holiday on Memorial Day and Labor Day but do not stop work must also be calculated as double wages; (5) Apprentices are required to be 16 years old as the standard. After three years of study, they can be promoted to secondary workers. The small accounts they receive should start at half a share and be increased as appropriate each year depending on the quality of their work. If there is no need to add apprentices, they should not be added at will; (6) Non-union members must not be hired at will, and union members must not be dismissed without fault. For any dismissal of workers, the capitalists must first report to the union. The dismissal can only be implemented after the union investigates clearly whether a dismissal should be made; (7) Kitchen scraps fees should be completely enjoyed by the kitchen staff and must not be included in the small accounts for public distribution.

Foreign Communist Party

Noulens Handed Over

The "North China Daily News" reported that the Westerner couple, the Noulens, were handed over to the Garrison Headquarters yesterday (12th). Unless the Swiss Consul recognizes them as Swiss citizens, they will be tried by a military tribunal. This city has already received a telegram from the London Police Department, stating that the Bray mentioned by Noulens has been found to be someone else. However, the Swiss Consul is still investigating whether Noulens is Swiss or not.

Today (13th), the Shanghai Municipal Police issued a special announcement about its arrest and detention, stating briefly that the order issued by the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court regarding the case of a Westerner man and woman of unknown name and nationality accused of illegal communist activities was executed on August 12. After arresting the two individuals on June 15, the police searched No. 235 Sichuan Road, No. 66 West End Garden on Hart Road, and Room 30C, Central Building, No. 49 Nanjing Road. Documents were seized in the house on Nanjing Road, proving that the place was the secretariat of the Pan-Pacific Trade Union, Far East Branch, and the Far Eastern Affairs Office of the Third International. Its purpose was to create a proletarian revolution in countries and colonies along the Pacific. It was found that the secretariat of the Pan-Pacific Trade Union was established in Hankou in the spring of 1927 after the Communist Party conference, and representatives from all over the Pacific were present at that time. Since then, the secretariat has always occupied an important position in communist activities on the Pacific coast. A total of 211 documents and 1,081 other books and letters were seized in the aforementioned four locations. There were English, German, Russian, Japanese, and Chinese texts, including 73 relating to communist activities in China, 18 relating to communist activities in Japan, 4 relating to communist activities in Korea, 14 relating to communist activities in the Philippines, 14 relating to communist activities in Vietnam, 10 relating to communist activities in the Malay Peninsula, 1 relating to communist activities in Taiwan, and 1 relating to communist activities in India. The expenses of the Shanghai branch, about 130,000 yuan per month, were also found. In the evidence submitted to the Second Branch of the High Court on August 8, it was discovered that the defendants had a total of five addresses, four telegraphic addresses, and eight rented postal boxes. The deposits in seven banks in China amounted to 47,500 yuan. In addition, a huge amount of foreign currency was seized in the aforementioned locations. The aliases used jointly by the two individuals were the Fantlucks, the Noulenes, the Moodes, the Lukes, and the Brays. In addition, there were seven or eight aliases used exclusively by the male defendant and one used exclusively by the female defendant.

Printed in England

Sun Yat-Sen Stamps Arrive in Shanghai

Totaling 120 Million Pieces

Effective September 1

The Directorate General of Posts of the Ministry of Communications, during the tenure of Director-General Long Dafu years ago, ordered 1.5 billion pieces of Sun Yat-Sen stamps from the De La Rue Printing Company in England, to be printed and delivered to the Directorate General in installments over a period of five years. The Directorate General also had seven posthumous portrait plates of the martyrs Chen Qimei, Huang Xing, Song Jiaoren, Deng Keng, etc., engraved at the British Printing Company and handed over to the Printing Bureau of the Ministry of Finance in Peiping to print new stamps. The Postal Directorate General has decided to implement the use of the stamps in the postal districts of all provinces starting from September 1. However, the official circular has not yet been announced. It is now known that the first batch of Sun Yat-Sen stamps recently printed by the British Printing Company, totaling 120 million pieces, packed into over 70 large boxes, arrived in Shanghai yesterday. The stamps are available in denominations of one fen, two fen, four fen, and two jiao and four jiao. The postal authorities are now distributing them separately and will issue new stamps together with the circular to the 23 postal districts across the country within the month, to be implemented starting on September 1. They can be found in all provinces, cities, and provincial capitals at that time. However, due to the urgency of time, it may be difficult to popularize the distribution quantity in each province and county. It is said that the seven new stamps of the martyrs printed by the Printing and Minting Bureau of the Ministry of Finance in Peiping are currently being printed. It is feared that there will not be enough pieces to deliver by September 1, so the implementation period will take some time.

Chinese Representative Already Appointed

Deputy Director of the International Labor Council

Zhu Maocheng Writes Letter to Yang Youren

The directors of the International Labor Council are re-elected every three years by the International Labor Conference. Since the establishment of the National Government of China, it has sent a full delegation to the conference every year, and this year marks the third year. At this year's International Labor Conference, the Chinese delegation made every effort to campaign. However, due to the historical relations in Europe, there were considerable alliances. As a result, China was not elected by a difference of only four votes. However, the members of the delegation all believed that given the large number of workers in China and the efforts made in recent years on international labor issues, China should have an appropriate position in the International Labor Council. Therefore, they expressed this to Mr. Thomas, Director of the International Labor Office, who agreed and introduced them to Belgium to discuss the matter. After the close of the conference, the chief representative, Mr. Zhu Maocheng, actively contacted the Belgian government. Yesterday, Mr. Yang Youren, the labor representative of this term, received a letter from Mr. Zhu Maocheng from Belgium, stating that as a result of the meeting with the Belgian government, China has been approved to be the deputy director of the Belgian permanent director of the International Labor Council. Through the Chinese government, China can now occupy a considerable position in the International Labor Council. If Italy can approve the increase in the number of directors in the International Labor Council, then the issue of China's representation in the International Labor Council next year will be resolved.

National Goods Exhibition Hall of This City

Handling of National Goods Certification

Provisional Measures for National Goods Certification Proposed

Our city's National Goods Exhibition Hall, taking this city as a major port for Chinese and foreign trade, and also as a flourishing industrial and commercial area, with numerous factories and shops, and complex and diverse products. Especially, cunning merchants and market speculators are mixed in, only knowing private interests and disregarding public morality, often transporting and selling foreign goods, secretly changing trademarks, passing them off as national goods, and even imitating brand names, which has a significant impact on the future development of national goods. In order to remedy this situation, it is proposed to handle national goods certification to prevent counterfeiting. The provisional measures for national goods certification of this city's National Goods Exhibition Hall, consisting of ten articles, have been drafted and submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and implementation. The articles of the measures are now recorded as follows:

Provisional Measures for National Goods Certification of Shanghai National Goods Exhibition Hall

1. Any manufacturer in this city who wishes to apply to this hall for certification that their products are indeed national goods shall comply with these measures.

2. The applicant shall submit a petition, along with samples of the products for which certification is requested, together with drawings, specifications, and trademarks, three copies each, for review.

3. The application shall state the following items, and shall be signed and sealed by the applicant or their agent: (1) Product name, (2) Trademark, (3) Producer, (4) Place of production, (5) Capital, (6) Factory name or company, (7) Raw materials, (8) Labor.

4. Each certificate shall be limited to one type of product.

5. The certification fee is temporarily waived, and only a handling fee of two yuan per item will be charged, to be submitted with the application. However, if the same manufacturer applies for certification for two or more types of products at the same time, the handling fee will only be charged once.

6. The products submitted for certification will be subject to on-site investigation by personnel dispatched by this hall. If they are deemed to meet the national goods standards stipulated by the Ministry of Industry, a certificate will be issued according to the grade.

7. In case of any doubts, the issuance of the certificate will be suspended. The handling fee will not be refunded. However, if there are special reasons, the producer may apply for re-examination.

8. All national goods certified by this hall shall be entitled to the rights under various preferential treatment regulations for national goods in this city, and may request to be forwarded to the Ministry of Industry for verification and issuance of the national goods certificate issued by the Ministry.

9. If there are any matters not covered in these measures, they may be amended at any time, and reported to the competent authority for forwarding to the Municipal Government for approval and record.

10. These measures shall be implemented from the date of submission to the Social Affairs Bureau for forwarding to the Municipal Government for approval.

A Hand Reaches In Through the Window

Wu Baoqing Assassinated

Wu Sits by the Window in the Kitchen

The Assassin's Gun Enters Through the Window

The Bullet Flies Out and Wu Falls to the Ground

Dead Upon Arrival at the Hospital

Wu Baoqing, from Jiangyin, formerly served as the head of the detective team of the Public Security Bureau in Jiangyin and Changzhou. After being dismissed, he came to Shanghai and lived at No. 854 Binlang Road, in the French Concession, where he ran a firewood shop for a living. At around 8:50 last night, Wu was sitting alone by the window in the kitchen, facing inward and with his back to the window. Suddenly, a hand reached in through the window and fired a gun at Wu's back. After the bullet flew out, Wu immediately fell to the ground. At that time, the second landlord, Jiang Jinsheng, was sitting in the living room and rushed in to check after hearing the sound. He saw that Wu Baoqing had fallen to the ground with blood flowing out. He immediately reported to the Gordon Road Patrol Station, which took Wu by car to Renji Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of his injuries, he was already dead upon arrival at the hospital. Examinations revealed one bullet wound in the face and one in the abdomen. The deceased, also known as Biao, was 34 years old. It is said that Wu had arrested communists several times during his tenure, and thus may have made enemies.

A Dancing Girl Covered in Feces

From Paris to Shanghai

Inevitably Makes Enemies in Paris

This Action is Someone's Directive

The Judge Adjourns the Hearing for Further Investigation

Sun Aiying, a dancing girl from a Shanghai dance hall, from Nanjing, residing at No. 552 Dagu Road, was riding in a rickshaw to the Shanghai dance hall at around 10 p.m. the night before. As the rickshaw passed the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Maohuo Road, Zhou Fugen from Wuxi, Qiu Genfa from Nanjing, and Ye Zixiang from Ningbo suddenly blocked the way. Qiu and Ye held the rickshaw, while Zhou threw feces prepared in a cigarette can at Sun, hitting her head and covering her face with yellow and white substances that smelled terrible. At that time, Sun's silk scarf and a pin were also missing. Sun then shouted frantically, and two Chinese constables, No. 2313 and No. 2398, arrived and helped chase them, and Zhou and the others were caught at Baker Road. They were taken to the Xinzha Patrol Station together and sent to the summary court of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. Qian Xunjiu, the patrol station's lawyer, explained the case and stated that Sun Aiying had previously been a dancing girl in a Paris dance hall and had just entered Shanghai. According to the patrol station's investigation, this incident was instigated by Ge Chongxi, the manager of the Paris dance hall, who instructed Zhou Degong, who then instructed the three defendants to commit this prank. Subsequently, Sun Aiying stated in her statement that she had been a dancing girl in a Paris dance hall without a contract. When the Shanghai dance hall opened, she entered into a contract with the Shanghai dance hall. Manager Ge Chongxi did not agree and insisted that she stay in Paris, agreeing to sign a three-month contract. Last Friday, the contract expired, and she left Paris and entered Shanghai. When she left, Ge Chongxi told her companion Wang Xiuying that he would make things difficult for her. Now he has resorted to this vicious attack, which is due to two reasons: (1) He hates me for leaving Paris, and (2) Ge had previously harassed me, but I refused. These two reasons have caused today's incident. But I am a weak woman who relies on my business to make a living while I am young. If he continues to make trouble, then my future will be unimaginable. I request a strict investigation. Subsequently, Wang Xiuying stated in her statement that she, Sun Aiying, and Chen Huiying left Paris at the same time. When I resigned to Ge Chongxi, Ge said that if Sun Aiying left alone, I would not harm her at all. Now that you four are leaving at the same time, I will break her legs so that she cannot make a living. Now that this has happened, our future is extremely dangerous. Chen Huiying also submitted a statement to testify, and her words were the same as Wang's. When questioned, the three defendants all claimed that they were instructed by Zhou Degong. At this point, Sun Aiying stated again that the second defendant, Qiu Genfa, was a waiter in Paris and therefore knew me. Presiding Judge Cheng Shangfeng verified the statements and considered that this case was instigated by Ge Chongxi and Zhou Degong and that the two should be summoned to court. He then ordered the case to be adjourned pending the summons of Ge Xichong and Zhou Degong for investigation.

The Fall of Pu Jinghong, a Shanghai Beauty

Death Due to Heart Attack from Burns

The Old Mother Cries and Faints

Pu Jinghong, also named Kunying, a Suzhou woman, a singing and dancing queen and movie actress residing on the upper floor of No. 43 Fuchang Lane, Xiafei Road, French Concession, was only seventeen years old this year. In the afternoon the other day, after finishing filming a talkie at the Tianyi Film Company at No. 232 Gansidong Road in the French Concession, she asked the photographer to take additional stills. She went to the makeup room to get her hair permed. Due to a momentary oversight, the alcohol in the hair perm exploded and burned her head, face, hands, and feet. She was sent to Renji Hospital. Due to burns attacking her heart, she died at 2:40 a.m. yesterday despite treatment. The hospital reported the incident to the Shanzhong Road Patrol Station, which dispatched detectives to move the body to the Tongren Fuyuan branch morgue for examination. The head of the patrol station approved. Subsequently, Tianyi Company, in view of the poverty of the family, gave 500 yuan for funeral expenses, and clothing and a coffin were prepared in the afternoon for collecting the body, which was temporarily placed in the guild hall. When the body was collected, the corpse's mother mourned her daughter's tragic death and fainted. She was awakened by neighbors and was taken home by car. But Pu's father passed away last month, and the day of Kunying's accident happened to be the fifth seven-day period after his death. The unexpected tragedy is extremely painful.

Ren Kebin

Divorce Due to Wife's Adultery

The Wife Raises Questions in Prison

Still a Lingering Affection After the Divorce

Ren Kebin from Qingpu, has been working as a manager at the Yu Xin Pawnshop on Gudian Road. On the third day of the tenth month of the lunar calendar in 1927, he married Chen, the daughter of Chen, a fellow villager. They had two children, both of whom died prematurely. This spring, Ren rented a house on the upper floor of a sock factory at No. 4 Juxing Lane, Nine Acres, Xiaobeimen. Due to the nature of Ren's work, he did not often return home at night. However, Chen was young, beautiful, and also lewd. Unable to bear sleeping alone, she secretly became acquainted with Zhu Baoshan. Their secret meetings were not just a matter of days. On September 9 of this year, Zhu went to Chen's place for a tryst again, which happened to be discovered by Ren upon returning home. Helpless, Ren was weak and did not argue with her. He only drove Zhu away and advised his wife to change her ways. Unexpectedly, the woman was passionate about her affair and invited Zhu home again on the 12th to continue their pleasure. By coincidence, Ren saw them again upon returning home. So, he could no longer bear it and confronted her and drove Zhu out. Zhu, ashamed and angry, returned with a sharp knife and committed the crime on the spot. Ren reported the incident to the police, who arrested Zhu and Chen and took them to court. After the interrogation, the adultery was confirmed. As a result, the adulterer and adulteress were each sentenced to two months of imprisonment and sent to prison to serve their sentences. Now, Ren Kebin, because Chen had committed adultery several times, making it difficult to live together, hired lawyer Liu Xiang to apply to the conciliation office of the district court for divorce. Yesterday, Judge Chen Bingxin opened the court for conciliation and sent a letter to the Second Prison to have Ren Chen brought to the court. First, Ren Kebin stated that he was 26 years old and currently lived at No. 5 Dapu Lane, Dapu Bridge, and stated the previous circumstances, requesting permission to divorce. Next, Ren Chen stated that she was 25 years old and did not want a divorce. (Question) When will your sentence be completed? (Answer) It will be completed on September 18, but I am currently four months pregnant. At this point, Ren Kebin said, This pregnancy is not mine, and I cannot admit it. The judge obtained the statement and repeatedly enlightened the two parties. As a result, Ren Kebin paid Ren Chen 30 yuan for the expenses during her childbirth, and the marriage was allowed to be dissolved. The judge drafted a reconciliation record in court and ordered the two parties to sign and leave the court. Ren Chen was taken back by the prison guard for execution of the sentence. After leaving the court, Ren gave his wife a silver dollar for pocket money and four or five packages of food, and repeatedly told her a few words, reluctantly parting. At that time, the bystanders all said, Since you are so affectionate, why bother to divorce? Ren said that his divorce was a last resort and left after saying this.

Accusation of Husband Forcing Her to Be a Dancing Girl

The Special Court granted the request. Yesterday morning, the Criminal Tribunal, headed by Court President Xu Jia, opened the court for interrogation. On the police side, lawyer Ru Baoyi appeared in court. Zhu Tugeng stated that after his wife came to his house, she returned to her mother's house. On June 14 of this year, Zhang Awan's mother's house moved to No. 2 Honglin Lane, Kangti Road, and Awan returned home to take care of it. Unexpectedly, she left and never returned. He went to pick her up, but she did not want to go home. Later, he went to his father-in-law's house again, but they had already moved. After several investigations, he learned that they had moved to No. 1585 Changsha Road, and he went to negotiate and was able to take her back. But before long, she ran away again and was found and escaped again, and then surrendered to the Jiliang Institute. Her claims of abuse and being forced to be a dancing girl were all untrue. He now requests permission to take his wife back. Zhu Zhang Awan stated that on November 25 of last year, Zhu Tugeng struck her head open, and the scars are still there. Recently, he tried to force me to be a dancing girl but failed, and then stabbed me with scissors. Unable to bear it, I surrendered to the Jiliang Institute. Now I wish to spend my old age in the Relief Association and do not want to go home with my husband. Court President Xu told her that before a divorce is confirmed, the name of husband and wife still exists, and she should live with her husband and cannot stay outside, and the Relief Association is not a long-term plan. It is better to go home with her husband and be treated with kindness, and there should be no more violence. Her claim that she does not want to go home with her husband is not in accordance with the law. However, she firmly refused to comply. Zhu Tugeng's lawyer asked the court to make a ruling ordering her to return home. Court President Xu declared that a ruling could of course be made, but if she firmly refused to return, then this court is a criminal court and cannot enforce it. He should file a lawsuit in the civil court. He then ordered Zhu Zhang to return home with her husband Zhu Tugeng and that the Relief Association should not keep her. If she still did not want to return, the two parties could file a lawsuit in the civil court for a ruling. Upon hearing the judgment, she expressed her firm unwillingness to return home with her husband, and Zhu Tugeng also declared that he would file another lawsuit. The court then ordered that she remain temporarily in the Relief Association.

Municipal Public Instructions

Privately Operated Public Utility Companies

Purchasing Foreign Materials

Should Calculate in National Currency

The Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau believes that when Chinese merchants purchase foreign materials and machinery, the price is calculated in foreign currency. However, foreign currency prices fluctuate indefinitely. Although it can sometimes be cheaper, the budget will be greatly affected if losses are incurred, and there have been many cases of collapse. The responsibilities borne by various privately operated public utility companies in the city are to serve the people, and the relationship is very important, not comparable to ordinary merchants. Therefore, it is absolutely not allowed to take risks and speculate. Yesterday, it specifically instructed the companies, etc., that in the future, when purchasing materials and machinery from foreign countries, the price should be calculated in national currency. It should be explained before signing the contract, and they should be instructed to clarify this national currency price when quoting, and the time period within which it is valid, to avoid disputes when making a decision. The contract should be completely based on Chinese, and even if other foreign languages are prepared, they can only be used as attachments. Furthermore, for the sake of prudence, this purchase contract must be reported to the bureau. If there is a loss in the exchange of Chinese and foreign currency, it must not be included in the company's accounts and should be borne by the person in charge.

Jiangsu Flood Relief Association Begs for Rescue Telegram

Submitting a Telegram to the Central Government

The Jiangsu Flood Relief Association sent a telegram to the Executive Yuan, the Control Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Finance, and the Relief Committee, saying: To the esteemed Executive Yuan, the Control Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Finance, and the Relief Committee of the National Government, Unfortunately, Jiangsu Province has reported another serious disaster. Floods are rampant, causing damage in more than 40 counties. All areas along the Yangtze River, the Grand Canal, and the coastal areas, extending over a thousand miles, have suffered. Crops are submerged, and people and livestock are drifting in the rivers and rising tides. Houses are swept away by huge waves, and lakes and rivers are connected, causing panic among the people. Moreover, the three lakes roar together, and the three dams are opened at the same time, destroying thousands of embankment dikes in an instant. The human tragedy is extreme, and it is a rare sight in a century. The affected victims have no place to live, clinging to the tops of trees and the edges of mounds, building nests on wooden frames, exposed to wind and rain, and unable to call for help. If relief is not provided urgently, they will inevitably end up in ditches. We are heartbroken by what we have seen and are at a loss. To implement benevolent governance and provide relief, we can only rely on the national treasury. We earnestly implore you to consider the magnitude of the disaster, which concerns the vitality of the nation, and quickly allocate huge sums for urgent relief to save more lives, which will cultivate more vitality for the country. Emergency treatment is a matter of urgency, and it is by no means comparable to passivity. We hope for compassion and are overcome with anxiety. Wang Zhen, Huang Qinglan, and Cheng Jingsheng of the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association Preparation Office, bow, Wen.

Internal Approval

Exemption of Business Tax for Doctors and Hospitals

National Doctors Federation's Letter Requesting Verification

The National Doctors Federation has repeatedly received letters from doctors' associations in Wuhan, Wujin, and other places, stating that local business tax bureaus have levied business tax on doctors. After deliberation at a meeting, it was decided that doctors' groups are a type of freelance profession and are not within the scope of business tax collection. It has been submitted to the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Interior, and the Department of Health for protest. It is now heard that the association has received Public Letter No. 40 from the Ministry of Interior, which has been approved. The reply is copied as follows: "Regarding the case submitted earlier requesting exemption from business tax for doctors, it has been approved and a letter has been sent to the Ministry of Finance for verification and handling. Now, it has been replied that doctors and hospital clinics are a type of freelance professional and are not within the scope of business tax collection, and approval has been notified, etc. Accordingly, a letter is sent for verification." It is heard that the association has copied and sent the public letter from the Ministry of Interior to doctors in various places for verification.

Social Affairs Bureau

Preventing Abuses in Sending Back Impoverished People

Old Certificates Invalid at the End of the Month, Five Items Added to New Certificates

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, in order to send impoverished people stranded in Shanghai back to their hometowns, previously ordered the issuance of free travel certificates and consulted with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Shipping Association to handle the matter. Recently, it has been reported that some unemployed vagrants in the special zone are impersonating soldiers and holding the aforementioned free certificates, soliciting assistance from merchants and people. Ignorant people are often deceived. It is requested that the situation be stopped. After sending personnel to investigate, it was confirmed that this kind of fraud and extortion is illegal and should be prevented. All the aforementioned free certificates will be invalidated at the end of August this year. From September 1st, new certificates will be used, and the following will be added to the new certificates: "(1) This certificate is limited to one person for one-time use, and should be handed over to the crew for cancellation when verifying the ticket; (2) This certificate is only allowed to ride in the steerage class, and if there is no steerage class, take the third-class cabin; (3) The use of this certificate is limited to the ship name and date written on the certificate, and will be invalidated after the expiration date; (4) Certificate holders are not allowed to solicit money from others; (5) If there is any violation of the above regulations, they are allowed to be handed over to the local police station for investigation by the bureau." Letters have been sent to the Public Security Bureau, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and the Shipping Association for verification.

Resolution of Treatment Conditions in the Piano Industry

Generally Increase Wages Separately

Regulate Working Hours

The piano industry workers in this city requested an increase in wages and the establishment of labor welfare undertakings, and submitted treatment conditions. After self-negotiation and five mediations convened by the Social Affairs Bureau, fifteen articles were signed, and wages were generally increased separately. The mediation situation and the original text of the conditions are recorded below.

Mediation Situation: At 10:00 AM yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau convened the Mediation Committee to re-mediate the treatment conditions of the piano industry. Representatives of the Piano Industry Guild, Wang Wenkui and Qi Fusheng, and representatives of the Piano Industry Workers' Union, Jiang Xiangcai and Wang Caibing, attended. The chairman of the Social Affairs Bureau, Gu Bingyuan, presided over the meeting. The two sides argued fiercely on the fourth article on wages, the fifth article on worker welfare, and the second article on working hours. After the chairman repeatedly tried to enlighten them, the two sides finally agreed and signed the resolution in the afternoon.

Treatment Conditions: The treatment conditions of the piano industry are as follows: (1) Both parties acknowledge that the union has the right to represent all members; (2) The employer shall not dismiss workers without reason. If there is a reason for dismissal, the union must be notified first; (3) When hiring workers, the employer shall give priority to hiring union members; (4) The wage increase standard for daily workers is as follows: those with a monthly wage of 10 yuan or less will be increased by 3 yuan, those with 11 yuan to 20 yuan will be increased by 2 yuan, and those with 21 yuan to 30 yuan will be increased by 1 yuan. The wage for piecework will be handled according to the original standard; (5) The employer acknowledges a subsidy of 5 yuan per factory per month for the union's welfare undertaking expenses. Representatives of both labor and management will each select three representatives to form a worker welfare undertaking committee to manage the funds and be responsible for carrying out worker welfare undertakings; (6) Working hours: from March to August, the monthly working hours are stipulated as 10 hours, and from September to February, the monthly working hours are stipulated as 9 hours; (7) For commemorative days when the government expressly orders holidays, wages will be paid as usual, and piecework wages will be 1 yuan per day. If the party department orders the holding of citizen congresses and commemorative meetings, etc., each factory may send two representatives to participate, and wages will be paid as usual. Daily workers will rest on the 1st and 15th of each month, and wages will be paid as usual. If they work as usual, wages will be doubled, except for piecework. Daily workers will be given 12 special holidays per year as usual with pay; (8) Night work will be calculated as half a day's work for three hours and a quarter, and each person will be given 4 cents for refreshments, including apprentices; (9) The number of apprentices recruited by the employer shall not exceed one-third of ordinary workers. Those who are 16 years old shall be required to join the union (except for those recruited before the signing of this agreement); (10) The apprenticeship period for apprentices in each factory shall be three years. During the three-year apprenticeship period, a salary of at least 30 yuan shall be paid, which shall be issued upon completion of the apprenticeship; (11) If an apprentice becomes ill during the apprenticeship period, the factory shall send him to the hospital for diagnosis and treatment, and the medical expenses shall be borne by the factory owner. During the illness period, he shall not be required to make up for the work; (12) The monthly salary for apprentices is 1.2 yuan in the first year, 1.8 yuan in the second year, and 2.4 yuan in the third year. After graduation, the salary in the first year shall be at least 8 yuan; (13) The wages of all workers shall be paid at the end of the month, whether big or small; (14) If there are any matters not covered in this agreement, both labor and management shall handle them in accordance with the worker treatment rules and worker service rules promulgated by the municipality; (15) This agreement shall take effect from the date of signing.

Liang Saizhen

Continuation of Trial in Camera Newspaper Case

No One from Camera Newspaper Appears in Court

Liang Claims the Newspaper Was Close to Extortion

Liang Saizhen, a female actress from the Star Film Company, believed that a news item titled "The Illegitimate Child of Liang Saizhen, an Unofficial History Outside the Silver Screen" published on June 20 in Camera Newspaper at No. 12 Parker Road damaged her reputation, so she hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to file a lawsuit against the newspaper and its editor in the First District Court of the Special Zone. After a summons, the case has been previously heard. Because the editor-in-chief of the newspaper, Li Muzhi, did not appear, it was ordered that he be summoned again. This has been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning was the date for the continuation of the trial, but no one from the defendant's side responded, and no lawyers appeared in court. Only the plaintiff Liang Saizhen and lawyer Zhan appeared. Liang Saizhen stated that the news about her in the Camera Newspaper on June 20, claiming that she abused her daughter and had a relationship with Xu Xinfu, was completely untrue. After investigation, Xu Xinfu is a staff member of the Star Company's branch, and she is an actress of the main company, so they know each other, but there is no relationship whatsoever. Furthermore, Xu is not specifically responsible for picking up and dropping off actors, so why is he being slandered for no reason? As for the daughter, who is now four years old, she is hired by her mother to raise her, and there is no abuse. After the newspaper published this inaccurate news, she immediately wrote a letter requesting a correction and also called to express her concern. However, not only did the newspaper not correct it immediately, but it also said that she should personally go to smooth things over, otherwise there would be many more news stories about her that would continue to be published. Observing its intention, it was close to extortion, so she hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit. Then, lawyer Zhan submitted a letter from Camera Newspaper to Ms. Liang as evidence. After Judge Feng Shide verified the confession, he ordered the case to be rescheduled for seven days and summoned Li Muzhi to court for questioning.

Xujiahui Observatory reported at 4:30 PM yesterday's weather forecast: Hot and cloudy in the Yangtze River basin, thunderstorms in the north, cloudy south of Manda Island, easterly winds in the East China Sea, and winds are undirected elsewhere. The typhoon in the Pacific Ocean continues to advance towards northern Luzon. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the port was 93.2, the lowest was 77.4, the highest on the same day last year was 87.1, and the lowest was 71.2.

Letter Received

Dear Sir, In the news column of your newspaper on the 13th, a news item was published about the election of the Women's Relief Association. After investigation, it was found that it was not completely accurate. The points of error are corrected as follows: It was found that districts 1, 2, and 4, etc., were formally established before August 1, districts 6 were established after August 1, and districts 7 were only established on the 12th. According to law, only districts 1, 2, and 4 had the right to vote. Districts 6 and 7 had no right to vote. When the two sides disputed, the representative of our party department immediately announced that districts 6 and 7 could not participate in the election, and the election proceeded as usual. The representative of our party department was present to supervise the election and did not state that he was not responsible for this election. The information in your newspaper is untrue and is specifically corrected. To Shen Bao, Secretariat of the Shanghai Special City Party Department, August 13.
